\"Kubernetes API server audit logging is implemented across multiple packages in staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/. The system comprises four main components:\\n\\n## 1. Audit Event Creation and Context Management\\n\\nThe audit lifecycle begins with `WithAuditInit` (audit_init.go) which initializes the audit context and generates/validates audit IDs for each request. The main audit filter is implemented in `WithAudit` (audit.go), which orchestrates the entire audit process by:\\n\\n1. Evaluating audit policy rules against request attributes via `evaluatePolicyAndCreateAuditEvent`\\n2. Creating an AuditContext from the policy evaluation results\\n3. Tracking request/response data through different audit stages\\n\\nThe AuditContext (context.go) is the central data structure that holds the audit event and manages its lifecycle through different processing stages (RequestReceived, ResponseStarted, ResponseComplete). Request and response objects are logged via `LogRequestObject` and `LogResponseObject` (request.go) based on the audit level.\\n\\n## 2. Audit Policy Evaluation\\n\\nAudit policies are loaded from files via `LoadPolicyFromFile` (policy/reader.go) and evaluated using `NewPolicyRuleEvaluator` and `EvaluatePolicyRule` (policy/checker.go). The policy evaluator matches incoming requests against configured rules and returns a `RequestAuditConfig` specifying the audit level and stages to process for that request. Policies support filtering by resource type, user, namespace, and other attributes.\\n\\n## 3. Audit Backend Dispatch\\n\\nThe union of audit backends (union.go) dispatches events to configured backends. Three main backend types are implemented:\\n\\n- **Log Backend** (plugin/pkg/audit/log/backend.go): Writes audit events to local files in JSON or legacy text format\\n- **Webhook Backend** (plugin/pkg/audit/webhook/webhook.go): Sends audit events to external webhook endpoints via HTTP\\n- **Buffered Backend** (plugin/pkg/audit/buffered/buffered.go): Batches audit events and sends them asynchronously to improve performance\\n\\nBackends are configured and instantiated in server/options/audit.go, where `ApplyTo` sets up the backend chain. The buffered backend wraps other backends to batch events before dispatch.\\n\\n## 4. \"Kubernetes API server audit logging is implemented across multiple packages in staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/. The system comprises four main components:\\n\\n## 1. Audit Event Creation and Context Management\\n\\nThe audit lifecycle begins with `WithAuditInit` (audit_init.go) which initializes the audit context and generates/validates audit IDs for each request. The main audit filter is implemented in `WithAudit` (audit.go), which orchestrates the entire audit process by:\\n\\n1. Evaluating audit policy rules against request attributes via `evaluatePolicyAndCreateAuditEvent`\\n2. Creating an AuditContext from the policy evaluation results\\n3. Tracking request/response data through different audit stages\\n\\nThe AuditContext (context.go) is the central data structure that holds the audit event and manages its lifecycle through different processing stages (RequestReceived, ResponseStarted, ResponseComplete). Request and response objects are logged via `LogRequestObject` and `LogResponseObject` (request.go) based on the audit level.\\n\\n## 2. Audit Policy Evaluation\\n\\nAudit policies are loaded from files via `LoadPolicyFromFile` (policy/reader.go) and evaluated using `NewPolicyRuleEvaluator` and `EvaluatePolicyRule` (policy/checker.go). The policy evaluator matches incoming requests against configured rules and returns a `RequestAuditConfig` specifying the audit level and stages to process for that request. Policies support filtering by resource type, user, namespace, and other attributes.\\n\\n## 3. Audit Backend Dispatch\\n\\nThe union of audit backends (union.go) dispatches events to configured backends. Three main backend types are implemented:\\n\\n- **Log Backend** (plugin/pkg/audit/log/backend.go): Writes audit events to local files in JSON or legacy text format\\n- **Webhook Backend** (plugin/pkg/audit/webhook/webhook.go): Sends audit events to external webhook endpoints via HTTP\\n- **Buffered Backend** (plugin/pkg/audit/buffered/buffered.go): Batches audit events and sends them asynchronously to improve performance\\n\\nBackends are configured and instantiated in server/options/audit.go, where `ApplyTo` sets up the backend chain. The buffered backend wraps other backends to batch events before dispatch.\\n\\n## 4. Audit Event Truncation\\n\\nThe truncate backend (plugin/pkg/audit/truncate/truncate.go) wraps other backends to limit the size of individual audit events and event batches. It implements truncation of large request/response bodies via the `ProcessEvents` method and `calcSize` function, preventing oversized events from being logged while maintaining configurable size limits.\\n\\n## Additional Components\\n\\n- `WithFailedAuthenticationAudit` (authn_audit.go): Audits failed authentication attempts\\n- `WithRequestDeadline` (request_deadline.go): Audits requests that exceed timeout deadlines\\n- `AuditHandler` (admission/audit.go): Wraps admission plugins to add audit annotations\\n- Metrics (metrics.go): Tracks audit-related metrics like event counts and error rates\\n- Format (format.go): Converts audit events to text representations\\n\\nRequest and response logging occurs at handler level in handlers/create.go, handlers/update.go, and handlers/delete.go, which call `LogRequestObject` to log the request body before processing.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}

 ],\n   364→  \"text\": \"Kubernetes API server audit logging is implemented across multiple packages in staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/. The system comprises four main components:\\n\\n## 1. Audit Event Creation and Context Management\\n\\nThe audit lifecycle begins with `WithAuditInit` (audit_init.go) which initializes the audit context and generates/validates audit IDs for each request. The main audit filter is implemented in `WithAudit` (audit.go), which orchestrates the entire audit process by:\\n\\n1. Evaluating audit policy rules against request attributes via `evaluatePolicyAndCreateAuditEvent`\\n2. Creating an AuditContext from the policy evaluation results\\n3. Tracking request/response data through different audit stages\\n\\nThe AuditContext (context.go) is the central data structure that holds the audit event and manages its lifecycle through different processing stages (RequestReceived, ResponseStarted, ResponseComplete). Request and response objects are logged via `LogRequestObject` and `LogResponseObject` (request.go) based on the audit level.\\n\\n## 2. Audit Policy Evaluation\\n\\nAudit policies are loaded from files via `LoadPolicyFromFile` (policy/reader.go) and evaluated using `NewPolicyRuleEvaluator` and `EvaluatePolicyRule` (policy/checker.go). The policy evaluator matches incoming requests against configured rules and returns a `RequestAuditConfig` specifying the audit level and stages to process for that request. Policies support filtering by resource type, user, namespace, and other attributes.\\n\\n## 3. Audit Backend Dispatch\\n\\nThe union of audit backends (union.go) dispatches events to configured backends. Three main backend types are implemented:\\n\\n- **Log Backend** (plugin/pkg/audit/log/backend.go): Writes audit events to local files in JSON or legacy text format\\n- **Webhook Backend** (plugin/pkg/audit/webhook/webhook.go): Sends audit events to external webhook endpoints via HTTP\\n- **Buffered Backend** (plugin/pkg/audit/buffered/buffered.go): Batches audit events and sends them asynchronously to improve performance\\n\\nBackends are configured and instantiated in server/options/audit.go, where `ApplyTo` sets up the backend chain. The buffered backend wraps other backends to batch events before dispatch.\\n\\n## 4. Audit Event Truncation\\n\\nThe truncate backend (plugin/pkg/audit/truncate/truncate.go) wraps other backends to limit the size of individual audit events and event batches. It implements truncation of large request/response bodies via the `ProcessEvents` method and `calcSize` function, preventing oversized events from being logged while maintaining configurable size limits.\\n\\n## Additional Components\\n\\n- `WithFailedAuthenticationAudit` (authn_audit.go): Audits failed authentication attempts\\n- `WithRequestDeadline` (request_deadline.go): Audits requests that exceed timeout deadlines\\n- `AuditHandler` (admission/audit.go): Wraps admission plugins to add audit annotations\\n- Metrics (metrics.go): Tracks audit-related metrics like event counts and error rates\\n- Format (format.go): Converts audit events to text representations\\n\\nRequest and response logging occurs at handler level in handlers/create.go, handlers/update.go, and handlers/delete.go, which call `LogRequestObject` to log the request body before processing.\"\n   365→}\n   366→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. \"Kubernetes API server audit logging is implemented across multiple packages in staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/. The system comprises four main components:\\n\\n## 1. Audit Event Creation and Context Management\\n\\nThe audit lifecycle begins with `WithAuditInit` (audit_init.go) which initializes the audit context and generates/validates audit IDs for each request. The main audit filter is implemented in `WithAudit` (audit.go), which orchestrates the entire audit process by:\\n\\n1. Evaluating audit policy rules against request attributes via `evaluatePolicyAndCreateAuditEvent`\\n2. Creating an AuditContext from the policy evaluation results\\n3. Tracking request/response data through different audit stages\\n\\nThe AuditContext (context.go) is the central data structure that holds the audit event and manages its lifecycle through different processing stages (RequestReceived, ResponseStarted, ResponseComplete). Request and response objects are logged via `LogRequestObject` and `LogResponseObject` (request.go) based on the audit level.\\n\\n## 2. Audit Policy Evaluation\\n\\nAudit policies are loaded from files via `LoadPolicyFromFile` (policy/reader.go) and evaluated using `NewPolicyRuleEvaluator` and `EvaluatePolicyRule` (policy/checker.go). The policy evaluator matches incoming requests against configured rules and returns a `RequestAuditConfig` specifying the audit level and stages to process for that request. Policies support filtering by resource type, user, namespace, and other attributes.\\n\\n## 3. Audit Backend Dispatch\\n\\nThe union of audit backends (union.go) dispatches events to configured backends. Three main backend types are implemented:\\n\\n- **Log Backend** (plugin/pkg/audit/log/backend.go): Writes audit events to local files in JSON or legacy text format\\n- **Webhook Backend** (plugin/pkg/audit/webhook/webhook.go): Sends audit events to external webhook endpoints via HTTP\\n- **Buffered Backend** (plugin/pkg/audit/buffered/buffered.go): Batches audit events and sends them asynchronously to improve performance\\n\\nBackends are configured and instantiated in server/options/audit.go, where `ApplyTo` sets up the backend chain. The buffered backend wraps other backends to batch events before dispatch.\\n\\n## 4. Audit Event Truncation\\n\\nThe truncate backend (plugin/pkg/audit/truncate/truncate.go) wraps other backends to limit the size of individual audit events and event batches. It implements truncation of large request/response bodies via the `ProcessEvents` method and `calcSize` function, preventing oversized events from being logged while maintaining configurable size limits.\\n\\n## Additional Components\\n\\n- `WithFailedAuthenticationAudit` (authn_audit.go): Audits failed authentication attempts\\n- `WithRequestDeadline` (request_deadline.go): Audits requests that exceed timeout deadlines\\n- `AuditHandler` (admission/audit.go): Wraps admission plugins to add audit annotations\\n- Metrics (metrics.go): Tracks audit-related metrics like event counts and error rates\\n- Format (format.go): Converts audit events to text representations\\n\\nRequest and response logging occurs at handler level in handlers/create.go, handlers/update.go, and handlers/delete.go, which call `LogRequestObject` to log the request body before processing.\"\n}\n","numLines":366,"startLine":1,"totalLines":366}}}

\"Kubernetes API server audit logging is implemented across multiple packages in staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/. The system comprises four main components:\\n\\n## 1. Audit Event Creation and Context Management\\n\\nThe audit lifecycle begins with `WithAuditInit` (audit_init.go) which initializes the audit context and generates/validates audit IDs for each request. The main audit filter is implemented in `WithAudit` (audit.go), which orchestrates the entire audit process by:\\n\\n1. Evaluating audit policy rules against request attributes via `evaluatePolicyAndCreateAuditEvent`\\n2. Creating an AuditContext from the policy evaluation results\\n3. Tracking request/response data through different audit stages\\n\\nThe AuditContext (context.go) is the central data structure that holds the audit event and manages its lifecycle through different processing stages (RequestReceived, ResponseStarted, ResponseComplete). Request and response objects are logged via `LogRequestObject` and `LogResponseObject` (request.go) based on the audit level.\\n\\n## 2. Audit Policy Evaluation\\n\\nAudit policies are loaded from files via `LoadPolicyFromFile` (policy/reader.go) and evaluated using `NewPolicyRuleEvaluator` and `EvaluatePolicyRule` (policy/checker.go). The policy evaluator matches incoming requests against configured rules and returns a `RequestAuditConfig` specifying the audit level and stages to process for that request. Policies support filtering by resource type, user, namespace, and other attributes.\\n\\n## 3. Audit Backend Dispatch\\n\\nThe union of audit backends (union.go) dispatches events to configured backends. Three main backend types are implemented:\\n\\n- **Log Backend** (plugin/pkg/audit/log/backend.go): Writes audit events to local files in JSON or legacy text format\\n- **Webhook Backend** (plugin/pkg/audit/webhook/webhook.go): Sends audit events to external webhook endpoints via HTTP\\n- **Buffered Backend** (plugin/pkg/audit/buffered/buffered.go): Batches audit events and sends them asynchronously to improve performance\\n\\nBackends are configured and instantiated in server/options/audit.go, where `ApplyTo` sets up the backend chain. The buffered backend wraps other backends to batch events before dispatch.\\n\\n## 4. Audit Event Truncation\\n\\nThe truncate backend (plugin/pkg/audit/truncate/truncate.go) wraps other backends to limit the size of individual audit events and event batches. It implements truncation of large request/response bodies via the `ProcessEvents` method and `calcSize` function, preventing oversized events from being logged while maintaining configurable size limits.\\n\\n## Additional Components\\n\\n- `WithFailedAuthenticationAudit` (authn_audit.go): Audits failed authentication attempts\\n- `WithRequestDeadline` (request_deadline.go): Audits requests that exceed timeout deadlines\\n- `AuditHandler` (admission/audit.go): Wraps admission plugins to add audit annotations\\n- Metrics (metrics.go): Tracks audit-related metrics like event counts and error rates\\n- Format (format.go): Converts audit events to text representations\\n\\nRequest and response logging occurs at handler level in handlers/create.go, handlers/update.go, and handlers/delete.go, which call `LogRequestObject` to log the request body before processing.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[{"oldStart":95,"oldLines":6,"newStart":95,"newLines":10,"lines":["     {","       \"repo\": \"github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes\",","       \"path\": \"staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/delete.go\"","+    },","+    {","+      \"repo\": \"github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes\",","+      \"path\": \"staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/patch.go\"","     }","   ],","   \"symbols\": ["]}],"userModified":false,"replaceAll":false}}

\"Kubernetes API server audit logging is implemented across multiple packages in staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/. The system comprises four main components:\\n\\n## 1. Audit Event Creation and Context Management\\n\\nThe audit lifecycle begins with `WithAuditInit` (audit_init.go) which initializes the audit context and generates/validates audit IDs for each request. The main audit filter is implemented in `WithAudit` (audit.go), which orchestrates the entire audit process by:\\n\\n1. Evaluating audit policy rules against request attributes via `evaluatePolicyAndCreateAuditEvent`\\n2. Creating an AuditContext from the policy evaluation results\\n3. Tracking request/response data through different audit stages\\n\\nThe AuditContext (context.go) is the central data structure that holds the audit event and manages its lifecycle through different processing stages (RequestReceived, ResponseStarted, ResponseComplete). Request and response objects are logged via `LogRequestObject` and `LogResponseObject` (request.go) based on the audit level.\\n\\n## 2. Audit Policy Evaluation\\n\\nAudit policies are loaded from files via `LoadPolicyFromFile` (policy/reader.go) and evaluated using `NewPolicyRuleEvaluator` and `EvaluatePolicyRule` (policy/checker.go). The policy evaluator matches incoming requests against configured rules and returns a `RequestAuditConfig` specifying the audit level and stages to process for that request. Policies support filtering by resource type, user, namespace, and other attributes.\\n\\n## 3. Audit Backend Dispatch\\n\\nThe union of audit backends (union.go) dispatches events to configured backends. Three main backend types are implemented:\\n\\n- **Log Backend** (plugin/pkg/audit/log/backend.go): Writes audit events to local files in JSON or legacy text format\\n- **Webhook Backend** (plugin/pkg/audit/webhook/webhook.go): Sends audit events to external webhook endpoints via HTTP\\n- **Buffered Backend** (plugin/pkg/audit/buffered/buffered.go): Batches audit events and sends them asynchronously to improve performance\\n\\nBackends are configured and instantiated in server/options/audit.go, where `ApplyTo` sets up the backend chain. The buffered backend wraps other backends to batch events before dispatch.\\n\\n## 4. Audit Event Truncation\\n\\nThe truncate backend (plugin/pkg/audit/truncate/truncate.go) wraps other backends to limit the size of individual audit events and event batches. It implements truncation of large request/response bodies via the `ProcessEvents` method and `calcSize` function, preventing oversized events from being logged while maintaining configurable size limits.\\n\\n## Additional Components\\n\\n- `WithFailedAuthenticationAudit` (authn_audit.go): Audits failed authentication attempts\\n- `WithRequestDeadline` (request_deadline.go): Audits requests that exceed timeout deadlines\\n- `AuditHandler` (admission/audit.go): Wraps admission plugins to add audit annotations\\n- Metrics (metrics.go): Tracks audit-related metrics like event counts and error rates\\n- Format (format.go): Converts audit events to text representations\\n\\nRequest and response logging occurs at handler level in handlers/create.go, handlers/update.go, and handlers/delete.go, which call `LogRequestObject` to log the request body before processing.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[{"oldStart":311,"oldLines":6,"newStart":311,"newLines":16,"lines":["       \"repo\": \"github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes\",","       \"path\": \"staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/request.go\",","       \"symbol\": \"LogRequestObject\"","+    },","+    {","+      \"repo\": \"github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes\",","+      \"path\": \"staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/audit/request.go\",","+      \"symbol\": \"LogRequestPatch\"","+    },","+    {","+      \"repo\": \"github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes\",","+      \"path\": \"staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/patch.go\",","+      \"symbol\": \"PatchResource\"","     }","   ],","   \"chain\": ["]}],"userModified":false,"replaceAll":false}}

\"Kubernetes API server audit logging is implemented across multiple packages in staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/. The system comprises four main components:\\n\\n## 1. Audit Event Creation and Context Management\\n\\nThe audit lifecycle begins with `WithAuditInit` (audit_init.go) which initializes the audit context and generates/validates audit IDs for each request. The main audit filter is implemented in `WithAudit` (audit.go), which orchestrates the entire audit process by:\\n\\n1. Evaluating audit policy rules against request attributes via `evaluatePolicyAndCreateAuditEvent`\\n2. Creating an AuditContext from the policy evaluation results\\n3. Tracking request/response data through different audit stages\\n\\nThe AuditContext (context.go) is the central data structure that holds the audit event and manages its lifecycle through different processing stages (RequestReceived, ResponseStarted, ResponseComplete). Request and response objects are logged via `LogRequestObject` and `LogResponseObject` (request.go) based on the audit level.\\n\\n## 2. Audit Policy Evaluation\\n\\nAudit policies are loaded from files via `LoadPolicyFromFile` (policy/reader.go) and evaluated using `NewPolicyRuleEvaluator` and `EvaluatePolicyRule` (policy/checker.go). The policy evaluator matches incoming requests against configured rules and returns a `RequestAuditConfig` specifying the audit level and stages to process for that request. Policies support filtering by resource type, user, namespace, and other attributes.\\n\\n## 3. Audit Backend Dispatch\\n\\nThe union of audit backends (union.go) dispatches events to configured backends. Three main backend types are implemented:\\n\\n- **Log Backend** (plugin/pkg/audit/log/backend.go): Writes audit events to local files in JSON or legacy text format\\n- **Webhook Backend** (plugin/pkg/audit/webhook/webhook.go): Sends audit events to external webhook endpoints via HTTP\\n- **Buffered Backend** (plugin/pkg/audit/buffered/buffered.go): Batches audit events and sends them asynchronously to improve performance\\n\\nBackends are configured and instantiated in server/options/audit.go, where `ApplyTo` sets up the backend chain.
